### Post by phrostbyte on 2009-08-01
**_Awesome August 2009 Screenshot Thread_**

[b][color=red]Use thumbnails for displaying your Screenshot(s). Thanks.
- Artificial Intelligence[/b][/color]


> 
* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
* To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-08-01
1. I am using xfce4-panel with it's pager plugin but last I checked, you could go into gnome-panel's pager applet's preferences by right-clicking on it and choose to, "show workspace labels", or something to that effect.

2. Yeah, it's conky. In my sig, there's one by the name 'conkyrsstemplate' which if you open with a text editor and scroll down, has something like the following:

###FEED 1 URL### ###FEED 2 URL###
###FEED 1 URL### ###FEED 2 URL###

Just replace the hashes and hash'd text with the URL of the feeds you want. Adjusting the rssbar for different screen resolutions is a tad more difficult, however.

As for conky being a tad abstract, keep playing around with it. I found it daunting as well but after trying screenlets as discovering *one bloodly desktop applet could use > 10mb of RAM*, I went back and forced myself to learn & love conky (and it's 1mb-per-instance footprint).

3. Yes, Eikon2, with a black folder mod by (I think) Sand and Mercury.



And Giant Speck: now that I've got a monitor with a decent contrast ratio, changing the murrine gradients and highlights was less an optional endeavour and more a measure to save my eyes. Oy vey. I almost feel guilty for subjecting people to my older screenshots.

---

### Post by spupy on 2009-08-01
> **Mark76 said:**
> Rox doesn't have a dock :?

It has the rox panel, is that what you mean? And if so... how did you manage to get it to be transparent?

I must have that :D

Yeah, sorry, it's not the rox panel. It's just rox icons ordered as a dock. It's just that - icons ordered to look like a dock, although the icons themselves function the same way as the icons on a dock (the OS X one, i think). For example, you click on the firefox icon, if firefox is not running, it will start. If it is already opened on another desktop or is minimized, it will bring it to focus. There are also some scripts to show some counts (like unread email & rss) in little blue dots on the icons (again, as the OS X mail app).

### Post by steelcap on 2009-08-01
> **coldReactive said:**
> It would ALSO be nice to know how that user got it so that the TEXT of the menu items DOES NOT get transparent.

See screenshots above - using alpha blur only effects the background of translucent parts of windows - without using this feature text will also be affected by the opacity setting.

### Post by coldReactive on 2009-08-01
> **steelcap said:**
> See screenshots above - using alpha blur only effects the background of translucent parts of windows - without using this feature text will also be affected by the opacity setting.

Anyway to get it to also blur behind metacity alphas?

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-08-01
> **coldReactive said:**
> Anyway to get it to also blur behind metacity alphas?

Alpha Blur should blur anything that has a transparent background. Go in Compiz Fusion, go in the Blur plug-in section, and make sure the text box that has "Alpha Blur Windows" next to it, has "any" in it.

[IMG]http://img213.imageshack.us/img213/5798/screenshotcompizconfigs.png[/IMG]

Also, keep in mind Metacity just lowers the opacity of the window, the lower the opacity, the less blur. So you may just not be noticing it.

---

### Post by coldReactive on 2009-08-01
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Also, keep in mind Metacity just lowers the opacity of the window, the lower the opacity, the less blur. So you may just not be noticing it.

gwd under apps in gconf-editor can edit the titlebar opacity.

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-08-01
> **coldReactive said:**
> gwd under apps in gconf-editor can edit the titlebar opacity.

Yes, same rules apply. 

Lowering the opacity of a window or part of a window also lowers the opacity of the blur for that said window.

---

### Post by sideaway on 2009-08-02
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Hah, TippedOut: given up on KDE again?

Nice. Details?

Sure,

Openbox w/o gnome or KDE, with Nautilus as a window manager. Onyx Theme.

Background is a default one from CrunchBang Linux.

Tint2 for the above Panel, Config:
```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT2 CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------
# For more information about tint2, see:
# http://code.google.com/p/tint2/wiki/Welcome
#
# For more config file examples, see:
# http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/3232/my-tint2-config/

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 7
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 0
border_color = #ffffff 18

rounded = 5
border_width = 1
background_color = #ffffff 40
border_color = #ffffff 50

rounded = 5
border_width = 1
background_color = #ffffff 18
border_color = #ffffff 70

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = top center
panel_size = 95% 26
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 7 0
font_shadow = 0
panel_background_id = 1

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKBAR
#---------------------------------------------
taskbar_mode = single_monitor
taskbar_padding = 2 3 2
taskbar_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_icon = 0
task_text = 1
task_width = 140
task_centered = 1
task_padding = 6 3
task_font = sans 8
task_font_color = #ffffff 70
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 85
task_background_id = 3
task_active_background_id = 2

#---------------------------------------------
# SYSTRAYBAR
#---------------------------------------------
systray_padding = 0 4 5
systray_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = sans 8
time2_format = %A %d %B
time2_font = sans 7
clock_font_color = #ffffff 76
clock_padding = 1 0
clock_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# BATTERY
#---------------------------------------------
battery = 0
battery_low_status = 15
battery_low_cmd = notify-send "battery low"
bat1_font = sans 8
bat2_font = sans 6
battery_font_color = #ffffff 76
battery_padding = 1 0
battery_background_id = 0


#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = toggle
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```
Conky Config:
```
# conky configuration
#
# The list of variables has been removed from this file in favour
# of keeping the documentation more maintainable.
# Check http://conky.sf.net for an up-to-date-list.
#
# For ideas about how to modify conky, please see:
# http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/59/my-conky-config/
#
# For help with conky, please see:
# http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/2047/conky-help/
#
# Enjoy! :)
##############################################
#  Settings
##############################################
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Sans:size=8
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 200 200
maximum_width 240
draw_shades yes
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color white
default_shade_color
default_outline_color white
alignment top_right
gap_x 12
gap_y 12
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
##############################################
#  Output
##############################################
TEXT


${alignc 17}${font Arial:size=16}Hamish${font}

SYSTEM ${hr }
${voffset 2}Kernel: ${alignr}${kernel}
${voffset 4}CPU1: ${cpu cpu1}% ${alignr}${cpubar cpu1 8,60}
${voffset 4}CPU2: ${cpu cpu2}% ${alignr}${cpubar cpu2 8,60}
${voffset 4}RAM: $memperc% ($mem) ${alignr}${membar 8,60}
${voffset 4}SWAP: $swapperc% ${alignr}${swapbar 8,60}
${voffset 4}Uptime: ${alignr}${uptime}

NETWORK ${hr }
${voffset 4}Up: ${upspeed eth0} kb/s ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth0 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
${voffset 4}Down: ${downspeed eth0} kb/s ${alignr}${downspeedgraph eth0 8,60 789E2D A7CC5C}
${voffset 4}Upload: ${alignr}${totalup eth0}
${voffset 4}Download: ${alignr}${totaldown eth0}
${voffset 4}Local Ip: ${alignr}${addr eth0}

Hard Drives ${hr }
${voffset 4}Boot: ${fs_used_perc /home}% ${alignr}${fs_used /}/${fs_size /}
${alignr}${fs_bar 3,100 /}
${voffset 4}Windows: ${fs_used_perc /media/sda2}% ${alignr}${fs_used /media/sda2}/${fs_size /media/sda2}
${alignr}${fs_bar 3,100 /media/sda2}
${voffset 4}Games: ${fs_used_perc /media/sdc1}% ${alignr}${fs_used /media/sdc1}/${fs_size /media/sdc1}
${alignr}${fs_bar 3,100 /media/sdc1}
${voffset 4}Media 1: ${fs_used_perc /media/sde1}% ${alignr}${fs_used /media/sde1}/${fs_size /media/sde1}
${alignr}${fs_bar 3,100 /media/sde1}
${voffset 4}Media 2: ${fs_used_perc /media/sdb1}% ${alignr}${fs_used /media/sdb1}/${fs_size /media/sdb1}
${alignr}${fs_bar 3,100 /media/sdb1}
${voffset 4}Media 3: ${fs_used_perc /media/sdd1}% ${alignr}${fs_used /media/sdd1}/${fs_size /media/sdd1}
${alignr}${fs_bar 3,100 /media/sdd1}
```

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-08-04
> **cc8balla said:**
> Using a mish mash of ideas and a great wallpaper from this thread (<3 whoever posted it, can't remember atm), still using Crunchbang, Openbox, and Conky compiled with imlib2 support so I can display album art in conky.

Woah! Woah! Woah! Google Chrome (for Linux) really looks like that!? How do I install it (with Flash too)!? 

Please tell me.

---

### Post by cc8balla on 2009-08-04
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Woah! Woah! Woah! Google Chrome (for Linux) really looks like that!? How do I install it (with Flash too)!? 

Please tell me.

Well, it has support now for gtk themes so there is an option in Options >Personal Stuff >Set to GTK theme. 

Then just right click on the titlebar and make sure that Use System Title Bar and borders is unchecked. 

I am using the daily ppa for it as well, so it is as close to bleeding edge as I can get at least.

And to use flash (it is still unstable though, and itll crash randomly) start the browser by using:

```
chromium-browser --enable-plugins
```

### Post by Islington on 2009-08-05
> **hyperdude111 said:**
> How did you get that menu at the top?

Its a resized panel, that windows can cover, which contains the activity bar plasmoid.

The three things on there, are my 3 activities. I find this a much better way of using activites rather than having to zoom out then back in.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-08-05
> **sertse said:**
> How to take a Screen(shot)?

'print screen' as has already been suggested, or you could use a terminal program like scrot, or even gimp has the option (the latter can be timed, as well).

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-08-05
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> 'print screen' as has already been suggested, or you could use a terminal program like scrot, or even gimp has the option (the latter can be timed, as well).

gnome-screenshot has a nice little gui, and if you're running ubuntu chances are you already have it. I believe it's in the accessories menu, or you can start it from a terminal with
```
gnome-screenshot -i
```

More variables can be found at "gnome-screenshot --help" :)

---

### Post by quazi on 2009-08-05
Shutter is a pretty handy screenshot tool, but it's not included in Jaunty's repositories by default (it is in Karmic).  It includes quick image uploading to free hosting sites, which is pretty convenient.

---

### Post by furuno on 2009-08-07
> **waqar said:**
> This is what I got. how do I remove the opaque navigation bars on my botoom panel.
compiz made transparent menus but how do I make the whole window transparent like some people have shown here?It's simple, you just go to the Advanced Compiz Settings > Select Opacity, Brightness & Saturation > In the Opacity tab click the New button > Change the value to say 90 > And type all in the Window field > Ok and you're done...

Just remember it's very important that you put in the value first, or else ou'll get a 100% transparency on all window (read: the windows vanish)...

Well, then here's my screenshot :
[[IMG]http://img194.imageshack.us/img194/6118/gambarlayar.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img194.imageshack.us/my.php?image=gambarlayar.jpg)

---

### Post by wirate on 2009-08-07
> **furuno said:**
> Select Opacity, Brightness & Saturation > In the Opacity tab click the New button > Change the value to say 90 > And type all in the Window field > Ok and you're done...

This gave nothing :(

### Post by mjheagle8 on 2009-08-09
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Really slick. How'd you get pypanel (or is it tint2?) to group tasklist apps by workspace?

in tint2 you can do it by setting ```
taskbar_mode = multi_desktop
``` in the tint2rc

### Post by racerraul on 2009-08-11
> **stanca said:**
> BTW,when will they release the OpenGEU 9.04.1?:confused:

From what I hear soon.  They do not have the resources other distributions have so while their efforts are ongoing, there is hardly a handful of guys doing it.

But while on the subject... most of the packages are complete.  If you go to their forums you can get the instructions to do a 9.04 upgrade from the repos.  However, some features that are holding up the release (new themes, geutheme to name a few) are not ready yet.  Finding Theme-ing help to give each release a new look is very hard.  Despite Darkmaster investing out of his own pocket to hire a good theme coder.

The way it goes sometimes... but hopefully more support will come their way.

I have been trying to learn .edj but not having any real coding experience it is hard for me to get the hang of it.  And the .edj editor is tailored to help a coder and not very user friendly from a design stand point :(.

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-08-12
Hey guys, if KDE was **slow** for you, I know why. It's Kwin. If you replace Kwin with Compiz Fusion it's literally 20x faster, even faster then Gnome. I hope someone out there takes my advice.

-**TT**

[[IMG]http://img36.imageshack.us/img36/8795/snapshot1rxx.th.png[/IMG]](http://img36.imageshack.us/i/snapshot1rxx.png/)

Do you have a process for this? :$

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-08-12
> **graaant said:**
> Do you have a process for this? :$

Yeah. It's really easy. :)

1. Go to System Settings.
2. Go to Add/Remove Software.
3. Search for "Compiz".
4. Install the first choice in the results.
5. Search for "CompizConfig".
6. Install the first choice in the results.
7. Go to System Settings.
8. Go to Default Applications, and under "Windows Manager" select "Compiz"
9. Apply the settings (it will now switch to Compiz) and restart your computer. 
10. Welcome to Compiz Fusion.


You can then configure Compiz Fusion to the way you like it, with CompizConfigSettingsManager, which you can find in start menu, under Applications< Settings.

---

PC-BSD doesn't have 4.3 yet, does it?  Anyways, PCBSD's is  OK, though it was a little buggy at the time.

Mandriva used to be the best with KDE (3.5 especially).  Maybe still is.

I still dislike the clunky look of it.  Even if it does run fast.

I used to be a KDE3 guy until I switched to Gnome. 

I'll give it another serious go some other time.

Hey Chemical, if you're willing to give KDE 4.3 another go, I know how to make things faster for you... and I think the solution is something you're going to like.

Kwin (the window manager for KDE) slows your desktop down by a lot (and I mean a lot). If you replace it with Compiz Fusion, your desktop will turn into Speedy Gonzales.

Earlier today I posted a simple 10 step guide (in this thread) on how to install Compiz Fusion in KDE. Follow it if you'd like.

Best of luck.

---

### Post by rubioo on 2009-08-14
Copy the following commands into a terminal and execute them to install the plugin.


> mkdir -p $HOME/.gnome2/rhythmbox/plugins/
cd $HOME/.gnome2/rhythmbox/plugins/
svn co [http://nedrebo.org/svn/rhythmbox/desktop-art](http://nedrebo.org/svn/rhythmbox/desktop-art)

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-08-15
> **MattDobson said:**
> That is awesome.  Thanks.  Works a treat, I just need it to fit the whole song name in now.

@ Tipped Out, no I dont.  Does it work in Crunchbag?

If you want to fit the whole song name into your Conky Rhythmbox script, you can use ${scroll}.  I use
```
${scroll 15 ${execp conkyRhythmbox --datatype=AR}
${scroll 15 ${execp conkyRhythmbox --datatype=TI}
```
to keep my artist and song name within a certain width.

EDIT: Just saw that you got your Rhythmbox plugin working, so nevermind! But just in case you were wondering, I'll leave this up!

---

### Post by wersdaluv on 2009-08-15
> **londonali1010 said:**
> I have to say, that *is* intriguing...How did you get KDE to use GTK and Compiz?
Uhm. 

System Settings > Appearance > Style > Widget Style : GTK+

As for Compiz, 
System Settings > Default Applications > Window Manager > Use a different window manager : Compiz

or you can just use fusion-icon :)


Nimbus is a very nice theme to use on KDE. It fits the rest of the desktop well.

---

### Post by Subban on 2009-08-16
> **DownTown22 said:**
> How'd you do that with the album art??

And, what's the icon set?

Last thing first, the icon set is area0.43 from [gnome-look]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/area.o43+SVG+Icon+theme?content=101979")

The album art trick, simple but fiddly is all. Find a wallpaper where you can tuck the album art behind, like the girl in mine. Load it into the gimp/photoshop whatever and snip out a rectangle where you want the album art and text to go. I used 600x200 into a new image (we are done with this one now). Then go into your new rectangle one and carefully cut out the person/thing you are going to tuck behind, paste that into another new image. This one should now have a transparent background so it just needs tidying up a little, run a eraser with a soft edge around the edges to smooth them out. Save it.

Go back to the rectangle and new layer, add a black>transparent gradient right to left in my case, then drop opacity to 25% (ish), I added 1 pixel line edges to top and bottom also, save it.

Now, in your conky, you need to make it transparent ofc, and position it roughly into place on the wallpaper and load in the background rectangle (the one we made a little darker) then fine tune the positioning.

Then get the album art loading and now we finally load the smaller piece we cutout of the actual item we are tucking behind and position it ontop of the album art :]

Illusion complete, and really it sounds worse than it is, should only take 15mins or so...

---

### Post by Subban on 2009-08-17
I'll post this here as a few people seemed to like the things I was doing with album art in conky.

I noticed that using the standard method of getting the album art in conky with:
```
${exec cp "`conkyRhythmbox --datatype=CA | sed -e 's/\\\//g'`" /home/user/.album}
```
Obviously caused the image to be copied every single update, typically once a second. This didn't seem ideal so I thought I would farm out the job to a script, it could check if the file really needed to be copied and then do it. Because we are only copying it once every few minutes (if you shuffle albums) or each 45mins or so, we can do more things. In the example I apply a sepia effect, but you could rotate, transform, blur or anything.

Anyways, script is posted here... [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7801595&postcount=8700](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7801595&postcount=8700)

There is also a shot of it there, I won't repost it here.

---

### Post by Islington on 2009-08-17
> **Rasi said:**
> Please some info... i never managed to set kde up like this.

Looks like shiki theme being used by the gtk+ style in kde with a bespin window decoration with colors set to match theme.

You have to edit ~/.gtkrc-2.0-kde4 file to point at the correct gtkrc (in this case shiki)

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-08-17
> **ajy0852 said:**
> Earlier, I was running Openbox in Gnome and someone suggested I go to Openbox standalone. I did for a while, but now I'm using evilwm. I'm not showing it here but I'm using a couple cli apps as well.

Wallpaper from Vladstudio, GTK is a modified version of the Dark Elementary theme from Gnome-look. Icons are Oxygen.

Lastly, there's the obligatory screenshot of evilwm and the Overglossed GTK theme.

> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> i like evilwm. i found it a lot more fun when using xbindkeys and gmrun with it. are you using either of those?

> **ajy0852 said:**
> Not yet, I may use xbindkeys to run a menu sometime. For now I'm OK running things from the terminal, and I'm not using it full-time.

I am really enjoying it, the only thing is that I tend to lose track of which apps are open on which workspaces. Is there any kind of a panel that does this? Apparently Tint2 doesn't recognize evilwm workspaces. This is all I'd want.

> **RiceMonster said:**
> I don't think there is a panel that recognizes evilwm workspaces, unfortunately.

I use evilwm quite often. Did you compile evilwm with vdesk support? vdesk is a nifty tool that i am pretty used to on my older desks that run just twm, and makes it easier for me to switch workspaces. 

Get vdesk, and compile evilwm with vdesk support. Then you can invoke vdesk command from a terminal and move windows from one desk to another. All you need is the hex id of the window that you wanna move elsewhere. This is where xwininfo or xprop come in handy.

Personally, the whole concept of panels, tint or otherwise just defeats the very purpose of evilwm. If you wanna have a slightly enhanced version of evilwm, with bar, clock support etc., then try badwm.

---

### Post by ssri on 2009-08-18
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Uh, except for the whole GTK/Qt thing, but I can only do so many things at once!!!

I do not know if it has been said here, but to make your gtk apps look nice in kde 4.3, you have to install gtk2-engines-qtcurve, kde-style-qtcurve, gtk2-engines-pixbuf.  Also, you should download (if you haven't already) oxygen-refit2 from gnome-look and sudo tar xvfz it in /usr/share/icons/.  Also, if there is an oxygen theme you like from gnome-look, extrat it in /usr/share/themes

then you edit ~/.gtkrc-2.0-kde4

here's mine:

```
# This file was written by KDE
# You can edit it in the KDE control center, under "GTK Styles and Fonts"

include "/usr/share/themes/Qt4/gtk-2.0/gtkrc"

style "user-font"
{
        font_name="DejaVu Sans"
}
widget_class "*" style "user-font"

gtk-theme-name="Qt4"
gtk-font-name="DejaVu Sans 9"
gtk-icon-theme-name="OxygenRefit2"
```

Start your gtk app, and it should be oxgenized :)

Although, for firefox, the tabs look a bit wonky, even after clicking the fix from system settings->appearances... I just looked for a kde4 theme on google.  Just drag the jar into your themes window and you should be set.

---

### Post by Islington on 2009-08-18
> **credobyte said:**
> Menu .. where I can get it ? :-k

Its the lancelot menu. It should be in repos. Unfortunately the version in the repos is not compiled with compositing support. To get compositing enable either build it scratch or install the packages from the repo mentioned in the bug report : [https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/kdeplasma-addons/+bug/408235](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/kdeplasma-addons/+bug/408235)

### Post by ssri on 2009-08-18
> **londonali1010 said:**
> OMG you are a lifesaver!!! I'd got so far as figuring out the first line of the .gtkrc-2.0-kde4 thing, but I couldn't figure out how to make the fonts look right...The rest of what you put looks great.  Now I use GTK+ widgets in KDE and it makes all my apps look consistent :)

Too make menus consistent while in superuser mode, copy your edited .gtkrc-2.0-kde4, rename it to .gtkrc-20.  Open up terminal, navigate where .gtkrc-2.0 and "sudo cp" (or sudo mv) .gtkrc-2.0 to /root.  If the theme does not look right, then you can install one of the kde4 gtk2.0 themes from gnome-look, kdesudo kate /root/.gtkrc-2.0 and direct it to use that one.

For those who hate kpackageit (like myself), you all can have a consistent theme when using synaptic. For myself, I mainly use apt from konsole to manage my packages.

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2009-08-18
> **ssri said:**
> Too make menus consistent while in superuser mode, copy your edited .gtkrc-2.0-kde4, rename it to .gtkrc-20.  Open up terminal, navigate where .gtkrc-2.0 and "sudo cp" (or sudo mv) .gtkrc-2.0 to /root.  If the theme does not look right, then you can install one of the kde4 gtk2.0 themes from gnome-look, kdesudo kate /root/.gtkrc-2.0 and direct it to use that one.

For those who hate kpackageit (like myself), you all can have a consistent theme when using synaptic. For myself, I mainly use apt from konsole to manage my packages.

Instead of copying the file(s) to /root, just use symbolic links instead.  That way, whenever you change your user settings, they are immediately reflected when running superuser programs.

Example:```
/root # ls -la
total 36
drwx------   6 root root 4096 2009-08-16 04:56 .
drwxr-xr-x  25 root root 4096 2009-08-16 01:57 ..
drwx------   2 root root 4096 2009-08-17 20:09 .aptitude
-rw-r--r--   1 root root 3409 2009-08-16 00:33 .bashrc
drwxr-xr-x   2 root root 4096 2009-08-17 20:09 .debtags
lrwxrwxrwx   1 root root   23 2009-08-16 00:28 .fonts.conf -> /home/daffy/.fonts.conf
lrwxrwxrwx   1 root root   22 2009-08-16 01:45 .gtkrc-2.0 -> /home/daffy/.gtkrc-2.0
lrwxrwxrwx   1 root root   18 2009-08-16 00:28 .icons -> /home/daffy/.icons
-rw-r--r--   1 root root  140 2007-11-19 11:57 .profile
drwx------   3 root root 4096 2009-08-16 19:13 .synaptic
lrwxrwxrwx   1 root root   19 2009-08-16 00:28 .themes -> /home/daffy/.themes

```

---

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-08-18
> **kenleyrob said:**
> Thanks! Although I can't see what you mean about blurred folders? do you mean the icons in the folder view on the desktop? I wouldn't call them blurred. I'm using green scrollbar and tabs to match the wallpaper and icons.

[EDIT] I see what you mean now, the small folders icons in the desktop settings window. I have no idea why they are blurred, I hadn't noticed that before!

It's probably the icon set. Perhaps the one you're using only has large icons that are scaled down for the smaller sizes, instead of small icons that are natively drawn.

GNOME has plenty of icon sets that are drawn in all sizes (gnome, tango, gnome-colors, erectus, breathe, elementary, etc.) I'm not sure why the stock Oxygen seems to be the only KDE icon set thoroughly developed for multiple sizes.

---

### Post by kenleyrob on 2009-08-18
> **perfectska04 said:**
> It's probably the icon set. Perhaps the one you're using only has large icons that are scaled down for the smaller sizes, instead of small icons that are natively drawn.

GNOME has plenty of icon sets that are drawn in all sizes (gnome, tango, gnome-colors, erectus, breathe, elementary, etc.) I'm not sure why the stock Oxygen seems to be the only KDE icon set thoroughly developed for multiple sizes.

That sounds like a reasonable explaination. I actually have had problems in the past with KDE icon themes not scaling correctly.

True, your suggestion would seem like a better option.  I tried it first.  However, for some strange reason the Qt gtk theme works perfectly under my user account, whereas it looks funny when using gtk apps as a superuser (i.e. synaptic). This happens even though both .gtkrc's point to the same theme directory in /usr/share/themes.  So, I use a kde42 gtk theme for those instances as a superuser and qt4 as a regular user.  Another reason is that banshee looks funny when using any of those kde42 gtk themes.  Anyways, it all boils down to the users system.

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2009-08-18
> **ssri said:**
> True, your suggestion would seem like a better option.  I tried it first.  However, for some strange reason the Qt gtk theme works perfectly under my user account, whereas it looks funny when using gtk apps as a superuser (i.e. synaptic). This happens even though both .gtkrc's point to the same theme directory in /usr/share/themes.  So, I use a kde42 gtk theme for those instances as a superuser and qt4 as a regular user. In your case, using KDE, you probably also need to link your ~/.qt and maybe your ~/.kde directories in /root.

Edit: Try just linking your ~/.qt directory first, then add the other if it is still a problem.

### Post by BslBryan on 2009-08-18
I've spent the last day or so setting up my girlfriend's desktop to surprise her. :)

Openbox with [AWN]("http://wiki.awn-project.org/"), [Icons of the Library]("http://samantha-wright.deviantart.com/art/Library-Icons-2nd-Ed-Windows-101728317"),[ Wallpaper, by Samantha Wright]("http://fc08.deviantart.com/fs47/i/2009/169/f/0/Old_Ink_Spill_Wallpapers_by_Samantha_Wright.jpg"), [Champignon]("http://www.dafont.com/champignon.font") conky font, and Times New Roman for everything else.  Openbox theme is Onyx (preinstalled).  

I love Icons of the Library very much, but just to let everyone know, you do have to build the icon theme yourself.  While it has several versions (Mac, Windows, png), none of these icon sets install themselves.  No matter what platform you use, if you want Icons of the Library, you've got to manually (tediously!) set them. :)

Click on the attachments for a more detailed view.

I was thinking of a tiling window manager for that kind of thing too, or for a program like GIMP - I usually have my toolbox on one size and my image window filling all the rest of the space on the screen. But it looks like a tiling wm doesn't respect those window sizes, it just distributes windows to a preset layout.

---

### Post by Rasi on 2009-08-19
> **ajy0852 said:**
> I was thinking of a tiling window manager for that kind of thing too, or for a program like GIMP - I usually have my toolbox on one size and my image window filling all the rest of the space on the screen. But it looks like a tiling wm doesn't respect those window sizes, it just distributes windows to a preset layout.

most tiling window managers can define layouts for given tags (workspaces) just make a dedicated gimp tag and set it up the way you like it. I have a gimp tag in wmii which makes the image itself maximized and keeps the toolbox floating above it.

---

### Post by Crunchy the Headcrab on 2009-08-22
Yeah I love the gimp.  I had a hard time using photoshop in one of my college classes after using Gimp for so long.  Photoshop just seemed overcomplicated and slow.  Still Photoshop is the standard but since I don't do enough graphic design to know any better I prefer Gimp.

---

### Post by yavez on 2009-08-22
> **Crunchy the Headcrab said:**
> Yeah I love the gimp.  I had a hard time using photoshop in one of my college classes after using Gimp for so long.  Photoshop just seemed overcomplicated and slow.  Still Photoshop is the standard but since I don't do enough graphic design to know any better I prefer Gimp.

I think I convinced myself that Gimp wasn't good enough, but anything I've been able to achieve with Photoshop, I've now been able to easily achieve with the Gimp (text kerning and the like is still fiddly, but not a major hassle).  The Gimp is faster too on my machine, handles the 60 - 100mb files I'm producing in a quarter of the time of CS4 on the Win7 installation I was running.  Just wish I hadn't dropped money on CS4 now :(

hinting=slight
subpixel order=RGB
Hope that helps..

### Post by itreius on 2009-08-23
> **Nevon said:**
> I seem to have the exact same settings as you, yet it looks like *** for me. What size are you using? And are you using the bold version or something?
gedit ~/.fonts.conf

Enter this and see if it helps.

```
<?xml version="1.0"?>
<!DOCTYPE fontconfig SYSTEM "fonts.dtd">
<fontconfig>
     <!-- Disable embedded bitmaps -->
    <match target="font" >
         <edit name="embeddedbitmap" mode="assign">
             <bool>false</bool>
         </edit>
    </match>
</fontconfig>
```
That should make all the Vista fonts (including Segoe) look normal.

### Post by bigbrovar on 2009-08-23
> **itreius said:**
> gedit ~/.fonts.conf

Enter this and see if it helps.

```
<?xml version="1.0"?>
<!DOCTYPE fontconfig SYSTEM "fonts.dtd">
<fontconfig>
     <!-- Disable embedded bitmaps -->
    <match target="font" >
         <edit name="embeddedbitmap" mode="assign">
             <bool>false</bool>
         </edit>
    </match>
</fontconfig>
```
That should make all the Vista fonts (including Segoe) look normal.

### Post by Rasi on 2009-08-24
> **davbren said:**
> Sorry I shoulda been more specific, I'm using KDE4. I can't work out how to install styles and icons for KDE...

styles should come with your distribution... simply install the one you want (e.g. skulpture)

icon themes can be installed via systemsettings -> appearance.
Keep in mind tho, that you have to tweak gtk icon themes to work with kde.

extract it. delete all fodlers except for the "scalable" one. 
Add a line saying something like "Inherits=Oxygen"
Copy the remaining theme to ~/.kde4/share/icons

### Post by OutOfReach on 2009-08-24
> **Felliph3 said:**
> 
Ah cool, my activity widget only shows Desktop, how to I add the other stuff?

Thanks!

Click on the cashew on the top right hand corner, select Zoom Out.
The desktop should zoom out and you should see a menu with several options, select Add Activity to add an activity and it should show up on your Activity Bar widget. To use each activity as a separate desktop, Zoom out then select Configure Plasma and select the first option which is "Different Activity for each desktop" and press OK

---

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1133123&page=12](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1133123&page=12) a few months back.

Xfce: 56mb immediately after bootup, xfce compositing was on. Not using Thunar was a interface choice, wouldn't really affect ram use. Xfce session is the only significant change, I really dislike xfce's session management, I prefer no management to it.

That was using Debian rather than Ubuntu though, but a Ubuntu minimal install could get similar results. Xubuntu ain't for ram battles :)

Anyway, this is a screenshot thread! If you got something you like, it's pretty and helps you compute, no reason not to run it if your hardware can handle it. :)

---

[attach]126185[/attach]

That's a 120Mhz Pentium running Musca as a window manager on Xorg 7.3. Crux 2.4 is doing the background work while hnb, tty-clock, vimwiki and alpine show off for the crowd. Memory profile is somewhere around 6Mb occupied of the 12Mb available. Swap space use is under 10Mb.

### Post by sertse on 2009-08-25
KDE 4 can be light!

KDE4.3 using only **105mb** after start-up. Debian net install, KDE-minimal, all bling disabled. I haven't looked into services yet, but as as it built from ground up, shouldn't be that much to tweak (but hopefully I can bring it lower!).

I don't feel I've ripping out essential functionally to reach this number. It does the same as it does on my xfce/*box set-ups I've kept wicd, yakuake etc because it convenient to me for example. 

KDE 4.3 really improved on resource usage. I dare say with good app selection, you can run it on 512ram without much issue... (This is a 1 gig netbook, but my usage never gets past 400 here)

### Post by Felliph3 on 2009-08-26
> **OutOfReach said:**
> Click on the cashew on the top right hand corner, select Zoom Out.
The desktop should zoom out and you should see a menu with several options, select Add Activity to add an activity and it should show up on your Activity Bar widget. To use each activity as a separate desktop, Zoom out then select Configure Plasma and select the first option which is "Different Activity for each desktop" and press OK

Good stuff, thanks!

> The most I've ever had was 9, because it was default in dwm and I saw no reason to change it. I always have 4 and that's plenty. 16 is just ridiculous. I doubt anyone would actually make use of that many.

When I had 16 I regularly had all 16 of them filled to the brim with window(s). Remember it was a single 1024x768 screen, and I was doing alot with the GIMP and hires images. I often had images spanning 2-3 desktops, or more if I'm working with high detail. Having to pan around all the time is annoying, so I chose to span my images across multiple desktops.

I have 4 right now and it seems alright, but I might change it to 6 or 8. I do have dual widescreen monitors though which helps loads.

### Post by moma on 2009-08-28
@davbren:
Hello,

Gnome-shell is guite interesting desktop scheme. One can create new desktops/workspaces on the fly. It is easy to start and organize application windows on the workspaces eg. by drag & drop. This feature is very nice and smoothly implemented.

Operations such as opening, minimizing and closing application windows are very gently and moderately animated which contributes to a professional look and feel. I've only used its default settings.

The toolbar at the top does really nothing yet. It is not possible to add launchers, shortcuts or applets to it. At least not in this version.

I also miss the GNOME's window overview list. I often loose my minimized  windows because there is no "Window List" applet.

I do not need or use the sidebar at all. 

The most important questions is: What to have where?

---

### Post by Copernicus1234 on 2009-08-29
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Screwing around with system-wide directories unnecessarily isn't very smart. If you setup a new account, just copy over your themes.

Strongly disagree. There is no danger installing in a system wide directory and its better for all themes and icons to be available to everybody instead of having to duplicate them all over the system for all users.

What if a theme is updated? Then I have to copy the updated theme to all users manually again.

I mean, feel free to do what you want, but personally I love the system wide themes. Its the way it should be.

One way to get the same functionality is to have symbolic links to the global theme directory from each users home directory. Then all the themes are available to all users too.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-08-29

> Strongly disagree.
Over that? God forbid we had something important to discuss.

### Post by stanca on 2009-08-30
Why have I the impression that KDE4.3 looks more and more like Win7?But I don't know for sure who mimics whom.;)

---

### Post by TheNosh on 2009-08-30
> **stanca said:**
> Why have I the impression that KDE4.3 looks more and more like Win7?But I don't know for sure who mimics whom.;)

people keep saying the first thing they thought when they saw win7 was "wow, that looks a lot like KDE 4.x" but the first thing i thought was "doesn't Xfce already do that?"

the way it displays active windows in the panel as just icons reminded me of the Xfce iconbox panel applet (though that doesn't combine quick-launch icons with running programmes like win7) 

my point is that there's similarities everywhere, and it isn't necessarily "mimicked" intentionally by either side. there's a saying in the literary field that goes like this: "there is no new literature being written only old literature redone"
is this because all writer's are plagiarists? no, but rather because we are all a product of what we have seen and heard. new ideas are merely a collaboration of old concepts into a different form. inspiration for any design including that of a desktop is taken subconsciously from things we've already seen and there is nothing wrong with that.

---

### Post by samjh on 2009-08-30

Sure, there are similarities, but only on the surface.

### Post by tjwoosta on 2009-08-31
> Just use omploader.org

Edit: Just looked it up, they have a 1GiB limit on filesizes... 

Ill second that, omploader is great. 

Its free, you don't have to sign up because its annonymous, and it gives you a bb code that you can copy and paste into any forums that gives you a nice clickable thumbanail. Plus the size limit is 1GB per file, thats definately enough for a simple image, no matter how big your screen is. I use it for all my screenshots, and none of them have ever been deleted or resized on me in the past year and a half that I have been using it.
